This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n    20→// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n    21→//\n    22→// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n    23→// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n    24→// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n    25→// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n    26→// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n    27→// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n    28→// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n    29→//\n    30→// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n    31→// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n    32→// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n    33→// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n    34→// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n    35→// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n    36→// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n    37→//\n    38→// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n    39→// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n    40→// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n    41→// availability.\n    42→//\n    43→// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n    44→// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n    45→// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n    46→// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n    47→// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n    48→// to master availability.\n    49→//\n    50→// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n    84→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n    85→\t}\n    86→\tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n    87→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n    88→\t}\n    89→\tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n    90→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"retryPeriod must be greater than zero\")\n    91→\t}\n This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n//\n// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n//\n// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n//\n// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n// availability.\n//\n// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n// to master availability.\n//\n// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. Local raft node sends\n// messages to the remote through peer.\n// Each peer has two underlying mechanisms to send out a message: stream and\n// pipeline.\n// A stream is a receiver initialized long-polling connection, which\n// is always open to transfer messages. \"## Leader Election Patterns: Kubernetes vs etcd\\n\\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election through a **lease-based mechanism** stored in the Kubernetes API server (etcd backend). The core implementation is found in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/`.\\n\\n#### Architecture:\\n- **Core Component**: `LeaderElector` (leaderelection.go) orchestrates the election process\\n- **Resource Lock**: `LeaseLock` (resourcelock/leaselock.go) implements the coordination.v1 Lease API resource\\n- **Interface**: `Interface` (resourcelock/interface.go) abstracts the locking mechanism with methods: Get(), Create(), Update()\\n- **Health Monitoring**: `HealthzAdaptor` (healthzadaptor.go) provides /healthz endpoint integration to detect leadership loss\\n\\n#### Election Process (leaderelection.go):\\n1. **Acquisition Phase** (acquire method): Loops with `tryAcquireOrRenew()` until successfully acquiring the lease. Uses RetryPeriod and JitterFactor for backoff.\\n2. **Leadership Phase**: Once leader, the Run() method invokes OnStartedLeading callback\\n3. **Renewal Phase** (renew method): Continuously renews the lease by calling `tryAcquireOrRenew()` at intervals defined by RenewDeadline\\n4. **Failover Detection**: Leadership is lost when lease renewal fails within RenewDeadline. The LeaderElector detects this by failed API updates to the Lease object.\\n\\n#### Failover Mechanism:\\n- **Lease Duration**: Candidates must wait the full LeaseDuration before attempting takeover (default 15 seconds)\\n- **Renew Deadline**: Current leader has RenewDeadline (default 10 seconds) to refresh the lease\\n- **Retry Period**: Clients retry every RetryPeriod (default 2 seconds)\\n- **Time-based**: Uses local clock comparisons, tolerant to clock skew via tunable LeaseDuration/RenewDeadline ratio\\n- **API-driven**: Leadership detection relies on Lease object updates in API server (stored in etcd)\\n\\n#### Re-election:\\n- When the lease renewal fails, the leader steps down and triggers OnStoppedLeading callback\\n- The leader record (HolderIdentity field) is examined by all candidates\\n- Once the lease expires, other candidates resume acquire() loops to become the new leader\\n- LeaderTransitions counter in the record tracks leadership changes\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election (Internal) + Lease-Based (Client API)\\n\\netcd uses a **dual approach**: Raft consensus for internal cluster leadership, and lease-based coordination for client applications.\\n\\n#### Internal Raft-Based Leadership (server/etcdserver/):\\n\\n**Core Components**:\\n- `raftNode` (raft.go): Wraps the go.etcd.io/raft library Node, manages Raft state machine\\n- `EtcdServer` (server.go): Top-level server managing cluster membership and leadership\\n- `rafthttp` (api/rafthttp/): Handles Raft message transport between cluster members\\n\\n**Election Process**:\\n1. The Raft consensus algorithm runs continuously among all cluster members\\n2. Members send heartbeats to followers; if heartbeats timeout, followers become candidates\\n3. Candidates request votes from other members; first to get majority becomes leader\\n4. `ensureLeadership()` method (server.go) periodically checks if the server is still the leader by verifying raftStatus().Lead matches its own MemberID\\n\\n**Leadership Detection**:\\n- `isLeader()` method checks if current member's ID matches Raft's Lead ID\\n- Raft automatically handles timeouts and elections internally\\n- The `updateLeadership` callback notifies when leadership changes\\n- Stats (LeaderStats) track leader health and election metrics\\n\\n**Failover & Re-election Handling**:\\n- `ensureLeadership()` detects lost leadership via linearizableReadNotify() - if this fails, leadership is lost\\n- Raft's election timeout automatically triggers new elections when leader stops sending heartbeats\\n- `MoveLeader()` and `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()` enable graceful leadership transfer\\n- Members maintain election term and log indices to determine leader validity\\n- Followers reject proposals from old leaders using term/index validation\\n\\n#### Client-Side Lease-Based Election (client/v3/concurrency/ and server/etcdserver/api/v3election/):\\n\\n- `Election` type (client/v3/concurrency/election.go) provides application-level leader election\\n- Uses the same **lease mechanism** as Kubernetes: stores election records with lease TTLs\\n- `Campaign()` method attempts to become leader by creating a key with a lease\\n- `Observe()` method watches for leader changes via etcd's watch API\\n- The `electionServer` (api/v3election/election.go) provides gRPC APIs for the election service\\n\\n#### Key Differences from Kubernetes:\\n1. **etcd Internal**: Uses Raft quorum-based consensus (guaranteed strong consistency)\\n2. **K8s**: Uses time-based leases (eventual consistency, requires clock synchronization)\\n3. **etcd Failover**: Automatic via Raft election timeout; leader failure detected within heartbeat timeout (~150ms by default)\\n4. **K8s Failover**: Detected when lease renewal fails; depends on RenewDeadline (default 10s)\\n5. **etcd Cluster**: All members participate in Raft consensus; leader elected by quorum\\n6. **K8s Deployment**: Any pod/component can be a candidate; no quorum requirement\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\nThe **Kubernetes** leader election (in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/) uses a simple, portable **lease-based approach** suitable for distributed applications that can't rely on shared cluster state. It's API-server-driven with tunable timeouts for different network conditions.\\n\\nThe **etcd** ecosystem implements **two-tier leadership**:\\n- **Internal cluster**: Raft-based with automatic consensus-driven leader election and fault tolerance\\n- **Application clients**: Lease-based election for compatibility with K8s-style leader election patterns\\n\\nBoth handle failover through timeout mechanisms (Raft heartbeat timeout vs Lease renewal deadline) and both support observing leader changes for event-driven leadership transitions.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":865,"cache_read_input_tokens":51557,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":865},"output_tokens":6,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3acec752-86ce-45e5-abcc-9ab05d0e5455","uuid":"eb217f08-2b3f-4b28-a35f-64c7c192f2d6"}
